	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Catalonia</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the Spanish autonomous community. For the historic political entity, see <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Principality of Catalonia</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Catalonia_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Catalonia (disambiguation)">Catalonia (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Autonomous area of northeastern Spain</div>

<p><b>Catalonia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>: <i lang="ca">Catalunya</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[kətəˈluɲə]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Aranese_dialect" title="Aranese dialect">Aranese</a>: <i lang="oc">Catalonha</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Occitan" title="Help:IPA/Occitan">[kataˈluɲɔ]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Cataluña</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[kataˈluɲa]</a></span>) is one of the 17 <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">Spanish autonomous communities</a> in the northeastern corner of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. Catalonia and the Catalan people are defined as a <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nation</a> in the preambule of the 2006 Statute of Autonomy, although it was rejected and modified by the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Spain" title="Constitutional Court of Spain">Constitutional Court of Spain</a>, which declared this definition without legal standing.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>}}<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Catalonia consists of four <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Spain" title="Provinces of Spain">provinces</a>: <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Barcelona" title="Province of Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Girona" title="Province of Girona">Girona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Lleida" title="Province of Lleida">Lleida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Tarragona" title="Province of Tarragona">Tarragona</a>. The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, the second-most populated <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_in_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities in Spain">municipality</a> in Spain and the core of the sixth most populous urban area in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-demographia_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-demographia-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It comprises most of the territory of the former <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Principality of Catalonia</a> (with the remainder <a href="/wiki/Roussillon" title="Roussillon">Roussillon</a> now part of France's <a href="/wiki/Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Orientales" title="Pyrénées-Orientales">Pyrénées-Orientales</a>, Occitanie). It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (<a href="/wiki/Occitanie" title="Occitanie">Occitanie</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> to the east, and the Spanish autonomous communities of <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a> to the south. The official languages are <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Aranese_dialect" title="Aranese dialect">Aranese dialect</a> of <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-estatut_langs_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-estatut_langs-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the late 8th century, the counties of the <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">March of Gothia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Hispanic March</a> were established by the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Frankish kingdom</a> as <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudal vassals</a> across and near the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> as a defensive barrier against Muslim invasions. The eastern counties of these marches were united under the rule of the Frankish vassal, the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Barcelona" title="County of Barcelona">count of Barcelona</a>. In the 10th century the County of Barcelona became independent <i>de facto</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 1137, Barcelona and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a> were united by marriage under the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a>. The <i>de jure</i> end of Frankish rule was ratified by French and Aragonese monarchs in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Corbeil_(1258)" title="Treaty of Corbeil (1258)">Treaty of Corbeil</a> in 1258.<sup id="cite_ref-Petit-Dutaillis2013_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petit-Dutaillis2013-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Principality of Catalonia</a> developed its own institutional system, such as <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Courts" title="Catalan Courts">courts</a> (<a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_constitutions" title="Catalan constitutions">constitutions</a>, becoming the base for the Crown of Aragon's naval power, trade and expansionism in the Mediterranean. In the later Middle Ages, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_literature" title="Catalan literature">Catalan literature</a> flourished. During the last Medieval centuries natural disasters, social turmoils and military conflicts affected the Principality. Between 1469 and 1516, the king of Aragon and the queen of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> married and ruled their realms together, retaining all of their distinct institutions and legislation.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Spanish_War_(1635%E2%80%9359)" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Spanish War (1635–59)">Franco-Spanish War</a> (1635–1659), <a href="/wiki/Reapers%27_War" title="Reapers&#39; War">Catalonia revolted</a> (1640–1652) against a large and burdensome presence of the royal army in its territory, being briefly proclaimed a <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Republic_(1641)" title="Catalan Republic (1641)">republic</a> under French protection. Within a brief period France took full control of Catalonia, until it was largely reconquered by the Spanish army. Under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Pyrenees" title="Treaty of the Pyrenees">Treaty of the Pyrenees</a> in 1659, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish Crown">Spanish Crown</a> ceded the northern parts of Catalonia, mostly the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Roussillon" title="County of Roussillon">County of Roussillon</a>, to France. During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> (1701–1714), the Crown of Aragon sided against the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a>; following Catalan defeat on 11 September 1714, Philip V, inspired by the model of France imposed a unifying administration across Spain, enacting the <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">Nueva Planta decrees</a>, suppressing the main Catalan institutions and rights like in the other realms of the Crown of Aragon. This led to the eclipse of Catalan as a language of government and literature, replaced by Spanish. Throughout the 18th century, Catalonia experienced economic growth, reinforced in the late quarter of the century when the Castile's trade monopoly with American colonies ended.
</p><p>In the 19th century, Catalonia was severely affected by the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">Carlist Wars</a>. In the second third of the century, Catalonia experienced significant industrialisation. As wealth from the industrial expansion grew, Catalonia saw a <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">cultural renaissance</a> coupled with incipient <a href="/wiki/Catalan_nationalism" title="Catalan nationalism">nationalism</a> while several workers movements appeared. In 1914, the four Catalan provinces formed a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Catalonia" title="Commonwealth of Catalonia">commonwealth</a>, and with the return of democracy during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a> (1931–1939), the <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_de_Catalunya" title="Generalitat de Catalunya">Generalitat of Catalonia</a> was restored as an autonomous government. After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist</a> dictatorship enacted repressive measures, abolishing Catalan self-government and banning the official use of the Catalan language again. After a first period of <a href="/wiki/Autarky" title="Autarky">autarky</a>, from the late 1950s through to the 1970s Catalonia saw <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle" title="Spanish miracle">rapid economic growth</a>, drawing many workers from across Spain, making Barcelona one of Europe's largest industrial metropolitan areas and turning Catalonia into a major tourist destination. Since the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spanish transition to democracy</a> (1975–1982), Catalonia has regained considerable autonomy in political, educational, environmental, and cultural affairs and is now one of the most economically dynamic communities of Spain. In the 2010s there has been growing support for <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_movement" title="Catalan independence movement">Catalan independence</a>. On 27 October 2017, the Catalan Parliament declared independence from Spain following a <a href="/wiki/2017_Catalan_independence_referendum" title="2017 Catalan independence referendum">disputed referendum</a>. The Spanish Senate voted in favour of enforcing direct rule by removing the entire Catalan government and calling <a href="/wiki/2017_Catalan_regional_election" title="2017 Catalan regional election">a snap regional election for 21 December</a>. On 2 November of the same year, the Spanish Supreme Court imprisoned seven former ministers of the Catalan government on charges of rebellion and misuse of public funds, while several others—including then-President of Catalonia, <a href="/wiki/Carles_Puigdemont" title="Carles Puigdemont">Carles Puigdemont</a>—fled to other European countries (such as Belgium, in Puigdemont's case).
</p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39"><a href="#Art_and_architecture"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Art and architecture</span></a>
