<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_pronunciation">Etymology and pronunciation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and pronunciation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name Catalonia—<i>Catalunya</i> in Catalan, spelled <i>Cathalonia</i>, or <i>Cathalaunia</i> in <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Latin" title="Medieval Latin">Medieval Latin</a>—began to be used for the homeland of the <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalans</a> (<i>Cathalanenses</i>) in the late 11th century and was probably used before as a territorial reference to the group of counties that comprised part of the March of Gothia and <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">March of Hispania</a> under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Barcelona" title="Count of Barcelona">Count of Barcelona</a> and his relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The origin of the name <i>Catalunya</i> is subject to diverse interpretations because of a lack of evidence.
</p><p>One theory suggests that <i>Catalunya</i> derives from the name <i>Gothia</i> (or <i>Gauthia</i>) <i>Launia</i> ("Land of the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a>"), since the origins of the Catalan counts, lords and people were found in the March of Gothia, known as <i>Gothia</i>, whence <i>Gothland</i> &gt; <i>Gothlandia</i> &gt; <i>Gothalania</i> &gt; <i>Cathalaunia</i> &gt; <i>Catalonia</i> theoretically derived.<sup id="cite_ref-Books.google.com_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Books.google.com-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> chroniclers claimed that <i>Catalania</i> derives from the local medley of <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> with <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, initially constituting a <i>Goth-Alania</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other less plausible or recent theories suggest:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Catalunya</i> derives from the term "land of castles", having evolved from the term <i>castlà</i> or <i>castlan</i>, the medieval term for a <a href="/wiki/Castellan" title="Castellan">castellan</a> (a ruler of a <a href="/wiki/Castle" title="Castle">castle</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Books.google.com_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Books.google.com-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> This theory therefore suggests that the names <i>Catalunya</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Castile_(historical_region)" title="Castile (historical region)">Castile</a></i> have a common root.</li>
<li>The source is of Celtic origin, meaning "chiefs of battle". Although the area is not known to have been occupied by the <a href="/wiki/Celtiberians" title="Celtiberians">Celtiberians</a>, a Celtic culture was present within the interior of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in pre-Roman times.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lacetani" title="Lacetani">Lacetani</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberian tribe</a> that lived in the area and whose name, due to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> influence, could have evolved by <a href="/wiki/Metathesis_(linguistics)" title="Metathesis (linguistics)">metathesis</a> to <i>Katelans</i> and then <i>Catalans</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Miguel Vidal, finding serious shortcomings with earlier proposals (such as that an original -<i>t</i>- would have, by normal sound laws in the local Romance languages, developed into -<i>d</i>-), suggested an Arabic etymology: <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">qattāl</i></i> (<span lang="ar" title="Arabic language text"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D9%82%D8%AA%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%88#English" class="extiw" title="wikt:قتالو">قتالو</a></span>, <abbr title="plural">pl.</abbr> <i><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">qattālūn</i></i> <span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic language text">قتالون</span>) – meaning "killer" – could have been applied by Muslims to groups of raiders and bandits on the southern border of the <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" title="Marca Hispanica">Marca Hispanica</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The name, originally derogatory, could have been reappropiated by Christians as an autonym. This is comparable to attested development of the term <a href="/wiki/Almogavars" title="Almogavars">Almogavar</a> in nearby areas. In this model, the name <i>Catalunya</i> derives from the plural <i>qattālūn</i> while the adjective and language name <i>català</i> derives from the singular <i>qattāl</i>, both with the addition of common Romance suffixes.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>In English, <i>Catalonia</i> is pronounced <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>. The native name, <i>Catalunya</i>, is pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[kətəˈluɲə]</a></span> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">Central Catalan</a>, the most widely spoken variety, whose pronunciation is considered standard.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> name is <i>Cataluña</i> (<small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[kataˈluɲa]</a></span>), and the Aranese name is <i>Catalonha</i> (<small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Occitan" title="Help:IPA/Occitan">[kataˈluɲɔ]</a></span>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Catalonia" title="History of Catalonia">History of Catalonia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cogul_HBreuil.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Cogul_HBreuil.jpg/220px-Cogul_HBreuil.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Cogul_HBreuil.jpg/330px-Cogul_HBreuil.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Cogul_HBreuil.jpg/440px-Cogul_HBreuil.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="295" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cogul_HBreuil.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Roca_dels_Moros" title="Roca dels Moros">Roca dels Moros</a> contain paintings protected as part of the Rock art of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">Iberian</a> Mediterranean Basin, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a></div></div></div>
<p>The first known human settlements in what is now Catalonia were at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a>. The oldest known trace of human occupation is a mandible found in <a href="/wiki/Banyoles" title="Banyoles">Banyoles</a>, described by some sources as pre-<a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> some 200,000 years old; other sources suggest it to be only about one third that old.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> From the next prehistoric era, the <a href="/wiki/Epipalaeolithic" title="Epipalaeolithic">Epipalaeolithic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a>, important remains survive, the greater part dated between 8000 and 5000&#160;BC, such as those of Sant Gregori (<a href="/wiki/Falset,_Tarragona" title="Falset, Tarragona">Falset</a>) and el Filador (<a href="/wiki/Margalef" title="Margalef">Margalef</a> de Montsant). The most important sites from these eras, all excavated in the region of <a href="/wiki/Moian%C3%A8s" title="Moianès">Moianès</a>, are the Balma del Gai (Epipaleolithic) and the Balma de l'Espluga (late Epipaleolithic and Early Neolithic).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> era began in Catalonia around 5000 BC, although the population was slower to develop fixed settlements than in other places, thanks to the abundance of woods, which allowed the continuation of a fundamentally <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> culture. An example of such settlements would be La Draga, an "early Neolithic village which dates from the end of the 6th millennium BC."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</a> period developed in Catalonia between 2500 and 1800 BC, with the beginning of the construction of copper objects. The <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> occurred between 1800 and 700 BC. There are few remnants of this era, but there were some known settlements in the <a href="/wiki/Segre_(river)" title="Segre (river)">low Segre</a> zone. The Bronze Age coincided with the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-Europeans" title="Proto-Indo-Europeans">Indo-Europeans</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Urnfield Culture">Urnfield Culture</a>, whose successive waves of migration began around 1200 BC, and they were responsible for the creation of the first proto-urban settlements.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Around the middle of the 7th century BC, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> arrived in Catalonia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Roman_and_Roman_period">Pre-Roman and Roman period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Pre-Roman and Roman period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg/220px-Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg/330px-Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg/440px-Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_Vilars_%E2%80%94_vista_sud-oest_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">Iberian</a> fortress <a href="/w/index.php?title=Els_Vilars&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Els Vilars (page does not exist)">Els Vilars</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arbeca" title="Arbeca">Arbeca</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg/220px-Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg/330px-Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg/440px-Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tarragona.Pont_del_diable_aq%C3%BCeducte.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Roman_aqueduct" title="Roman aqueduct">Roman aqueduct</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">Tarragona</a></div></div></div>
<p>In pre-Roman times, the area that is now called Catalonia in the north-east of <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> – like the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> side of the peninsula – was populated by the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>. The Iberians of this area – the <a href="/wiki/Ilergetes" title="Ilergetes">Ilergetes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indigetes" title="Indigetes">Indigetes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lacetani" title="Lacetani">Lacetani</a> (Cerretains) – also maintained relations with the peoples of the Mediterranean. Some urban agglomerations became relevant, including Ilerda (Lleida) inland, Hibera (perhaps <a href="/wiki/Amposta" title="Amposta">Amposta</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tortosa" title="Tortosa">Tortosa</a>) or Indika (<a href="/wiki/Ullastret" title="Ullastret">Ullastret</a>). Coastal trading colonies were established by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">ancient Greeks</a>, who settled around the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Roses" title="Gulf of Roses">Gulf of Roses</a>, in Emporion (<a href="/wiki/Emp%C3%BAries" title="Empúries">Empúries</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Roses,_Girona" title="Roses, Girona">Roses</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Colonies_in_antiquity" title="Colonies in antiquity">8th century BC</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthaginians</a> briefly ruled the territory in the course of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a> and traded with <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">the surrounding Iberian population</a>.
</p><p>After the Carthaginian defeat by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>, the north-east of Iberia became the first to come under Roman rule and became part of <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a>, the westernmost part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tarraco_(Tarragona)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarraco (Tarragona)">Tarraco</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Tarragona" title="Tarragona">Tarragona</a>) was one of the most important Roman cities in Hispania and the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">province</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tarraconensis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarraconensis">Tarraconensis</a>. Other important cities of the Roman period are Ilerda (Lleida), Dertosa (Tortosa), Gerunda (Girona) as well as the ports of Empuriæ (former Emporion) and Barcino (Barcelona). As for the rest of Hispania, <a href="/wiki/Latin_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin law">Latin law</a> was granted to all cities under the reign of <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">Vespasian</a> (69-79 AD), while <a href="/wiki/Roman_citizenship" title="Roman citizenship">Roman citizenship</a> was granted to all free men of the empire by the <a href="/wiki/Edict_of_Caracalla" class="mw-redirect" title="Edict of Caracalla">Edict of</a> <a href="/wiki/Caracalla" title="Caracalla">Caracalla</a> in 212 AD (Tarraco, the capital, was already a colony of <a href="/wiki/Roman_law" title="Roman law">Roman law</a> since 45 BC). It was a rich agricultural province (olive oil, vine, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>), and the first centuries of the Empire saw the construction of roads (the most important being the <a href="/wiki/Via_Augusta" title="Via Augusta">Via Augusta</a>, parallel to Mediterranean coastline) and infrastructure like <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(water_supply)" title="Aqueduct (water supply)">aqueducts</a>.
</p><p>Conversion to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, attested in the 3rd century, was completed in urban areas in the 4th century. Although Hispania remained under Roman rule and did not fall under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swabians" title="Swabians">Swabians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a> in the 5th century, the main cities suffered frequent sacking and some <a href="/wiki/Deurbanization" class="mw-redirect" title="Deurbanization">deurbanization</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg/220px-Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg/330px-Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg/440px-Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1339" data-file-height="980" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Origen_de_l%27escut_del_comtat_de_Barcelona_de_Lorenzale.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Origins of the blason of the County of Barcelona</i>, by <a href="/wiki/Claudi_Lorenzale" title="Claudi Lorenzale">Claudi Lorenzale</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, the area was conquered by the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> and was ruled as part of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> for almost two and a half centuries. In 718, it came under <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> control and became part of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>, a province of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>. From the conquest of Roussillon in 760, to the conquest of Barcelona in 801, the <a href="/wiki/Frankish_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Frankish empire">Frankish empire</a> took control of the area between Septimania and the <a href="/wiki/Llobregat" title="Llobregat">Llobregat</a> river from the Muslims and created heavily militarised, self-governing <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">counties</a>. These counties formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Septimania" title="Septimania">Gothic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_March" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish March">Hispanic</a> marches, a <a href="/wiki/Buffer_zone" title="Buffer zone">buffer zone</a> in the south of the Frankish empire in the former province of Septimania and in the northeast of the Iberian Peninsula, to act as a defensive barrier for the Frankish empire against further Muslim invasions from Al-Andalus.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/170px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/255px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg/340px-Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1072" data-file-height="1098" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Petronila_Ramon_Berenguer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Petronilla_of_Aragon" title="Petronilla of Aragon">Petronilla of Aragon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Berenguer_IV,_Count_of_Barcelona" title="Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona">Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona</a>, dynastic union of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a></div></div></div>
<p>These counties came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Barcelona" title="Count of Barcelona">counts of Barcelona</a>, who were Frankish <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassals</a> nominated by the emperor of the Franks, to whom they were <a href="/wiki/Feudatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Feudatory">feudatories</a> (801–987). The earliest known use of the name "<a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Catalonia</a>" for these counties dates to 1117. During the 9th century, the Count <a href="/wiki/Wifred_the_Hairy" class="mw-redirect" title="Wifred the Hairy">Wifred the Hairy</a> made its title hereditary and founded the dynasty of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Barcelona" title="House of Barcelona">House of Barcelona</a>, which ruled Catalonia until 1410.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg/170px-Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg/255px-Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg/340px-Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg 2x" data-file-width="547" data-file-height="763" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hug_IV_Empuries_Pero_Ma%C3%A7a_Croada_Mayurqa_1229.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hug IV, count of Empúries, and Pero Maça during the conquest of Mallorca (1229)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortes_Catalanas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cortes_Catalanas.jpg/220px-Cortes_Catalanas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="316" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Cortes_Catalanas.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="402" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cortes_Catalanas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 15th-century miniature of the Catalan Courts</div></div></div>
<p>In 987 <a href="/wiki/Borrell_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Borrell II">Borrell II</a>, Count of Barcelona, did not recognise the new French king <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Capet" title="Hugh Capet">Hugh Capet</a> as his king, making his successors (from Ramon Borrell I to Ramon Berenguer IV) de facto independent of the Capetian crown whom they regarded as usurpers of the Carolingian Frankish realm.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> At the start of eleventh century the Catalan Counties suffer an important process of feudalisation, partially controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Peace_and_Truce_of_God" title="Peace and Truce of God">Peace and Truce Assemblies</a> and by the power and negotiation skills of the Counts of Barcelona like <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Berenguer_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramon Berenguer I">Ramon Berenguer I</a>. In 1137, <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Berenguer_IV,_Count_of_Barcelona" title="Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona">Ramon Berenguer IV, Count of Barcelona</a> decided to accept <a href="/wiki/Ramiro_II_of_Aragon" title="Ramiro II of Aragon">King Ramiro II of Aragon</a>'s proposal to marry Queen <a href="/wiki/Petronilla_of_Aragon" title="Petronilla of Aragon">Petronila</a>, establishing the dynastic union of the County of Barcelona with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a>, joining the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a> and making the Catalan counties that were united under the county of Barcelona into a <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> of the Aragonese Crown.
</p><p>In 1258, by means of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Corbeil_(1258)" title="Treaty of Corbeil (1258)">Treaty of Corbeil</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Barcelona" title="Count of Barcelona">Count of Barcelona</a> and King of Aragon, of Mallorca and of Valencia, <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a> renounced his family rights and dominions in <a href="/wiki/Occitania" title="Occitania">Occitania</a> and recognised the king of France as heir of the <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">Carolingian Dynasty</a>. The king of France formally relinquished his nominal feudal lordship over all the Catalan counties, except the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Foix" title="County of Foix">County of Foix</a>, despite the opposition of the king of Aragon and count of Barcelona. This treaty transformed the principality's <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> union with Aragon into a <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> one and was the origin of the definitive separation between the geographical areas of Catalonia and <a href="/wiki/Languedoc" title="Languedoc">Languedoc</a>.
</p><p>As a coastal territory, Catalonia became the base of the Aragonese Crown's maritime forces, which spread the power of the Aragonese Crown in the Mediterranean, and made Barcelona into a powerful and wealthy city. In the period of 1164–1410, new territories, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Kingdom of Valencia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Majorca" title="Kingdom of Majorca">Kingdom of Majorca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">Sardinia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corsica" title="Corsica">Corsica</a>, and (briefly) the <a href="/wiki/Duchy" title="Duchy">Duchies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Athens" title="Duchy of Athens">Athens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Neopatras" title="Duchy of Neopatras">Neopatras</a>, were incorporated into the dynastic domains of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aragon" title="House of Aragon">House of Aragon</a>.
</p><p>At the same time, the Principality of Catalonia developed a complex institutional and political system based in the concept of a pact between the <a href="/wiki/Estates_of_the_realm" title="Estates of the realm">estates of the realm</a> and the king. Laws had to be approved in the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Courts" title="Catalan Courts">General Court of Catalonia</a>, one of the first parliamentary bodies of Europe that banned the royal power to create legislation unilaterally (since 1283).<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The Courts were composed of the three Estates, were presided over by the king of Aragon, and approved the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_constitutions" title="Catalan constitutions">constitutions</a>, which created a compilation of rights for the citizenship of the Principality. In order to collect general taxes, the Courts of 1359 established a permanent representative of deputies position, called the Deputation of the General (and later usually known as <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Generalitat of Catalonia">Generalitat</a>), which gained political power over the next centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The domains of the Aragonese Crown were severely affected by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> pandemic and by later outbreaks of the <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a>. Between 1347 and 1497 Catalonia lost 37 percent of its population.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 1410, King <a href="/wiki/Martin_of_Aragon" title="Martin of Aragon">Martin I</a> died without surviving descendants. Under the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_Caspe" title="Compromise of Caspe">Compromise of Caspe</a>, Ferdinand from the Castilian <a href="/wiki/House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="House of Trastámara">House of Trastámara</a> received the Crown of Aragon as <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand I of Aragon">Ferdinand I of Aragon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Reilly_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reilly-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> During the reign of his son, <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Aragon_and_Navarre" class="mw-redirect" title="John II of Aragon and Navarre">John II</a>, social and political tensions caused the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Civil_War" title="Catalan Civil War">Catalan Civil War</a> (1462–1472).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_era">Modern era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Modern era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg/220px-Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg/330px-Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg/440px-Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5781" data-file-height="4573" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cataloniae_principatus_1608.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">Principality of Catalonia</a> (1608)</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">Ferdinand II of Aragon</a>, the grandson of Ferdinand I, and Queen <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> were married in 1469, later taking the title the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Monarchs">Catholic Monarchs</a>; subsequently, this event was seen by historiographers as the dawn of a unified Spain. At this time, though united by marriage, the Crowns of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Aragon</a> maintained distinct territories, each keeping its own traditional institutions, parliaments, laws and currency.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Castile commissioned expeditions to the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> and benefited from the riches acquired in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonisation of the Americas</a>, but, in time, also carried the main burden of military expenses of the united Spanish kingdoms. After Isabella's death, Ferdinand II personally ruled both kingdoms.
</p><p>By virtue of descent from his maternal grandparents, Ferdinand II of Aragon and Isabella I of Castile, in 1516 <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles I of Spain">Charles I of Spain</a> became the first king to rule the Crowns of Castile and Aragon simultaneously by his own right. Following the death of his paternal (<a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>) grandfather, <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, he was also elected <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, in 1519.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_segadors.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Els_segadors.jpg/220px-Els_segadors.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Els_segadors.jpg/330px-Els_segadors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Els_segadors.jpg/440px-Els_segadors.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1814" data-file-height="1168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Els_segadors.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Corpus_de_Sang" title="Corpus de Sang">Corpus de Sang</a></i> (7 June 1640), one of the main events of the Reaper's War. Painted in 1910</div></div></div>
<p>Over the next few centuries, the Principality of Catalonia was generally on the losing side of a series of wars that led steadily to more centralization of power in Spain. Despite this fact, between the 16th and 18th centuries, the participation of the political community in the local and the general Catalan government was increased, while the kings remained absent and its constitutional system continued to consolidate. The <a href="/wiki/Reapers%27_War" title="Reapers&#39; War">Reapers' War</a> (1640–1652) saw Catalonia rebel (briefly as a <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Republic_(1641)" title="Catalan Republic (1641)">republic</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Pau_Claris" class="mw-redirect" title="Pau Claris">Pau Claris</a>) with French help against the Spanish Crown for overstepping Catalonia's rights during the <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years&#39; War">Thirty Years' War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Most of Catalonia was reconquered by the Spanish monarchy but Catalan rights were recognised. Roussillon was lost to France by the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_the_Pyrenees" class="mw-redirect" title="Peace of the Pyrenees">Peace of the Pyrenees</a> (1659).<sup id="cite_ref-pyrconditions_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pyrconditions-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most significant conflict concerning the governing monarchy was the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, which began when the childless <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_Spain" title="Charles II of Spain">Charles II of Spain</a>, the last Spanish Habsburg, died without an heir in 1700. Charles II had chosen <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a> from the French <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">House of Bourbon</a>. Catalonia, like other territories that formed the Crown of Aragon, rose up in support of the Austrian Habsburg pretender <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, in his claim for the Spanish throne as Charles III of Spain. The fight between the houses of Bourbon and Habsburg for the Spanish Crown split Spain and Europe.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Barcelona_(1713%E2%80%9314)" title="Siege of Barcelona (1713–14)">fall of Barcelona</a> on 11 September 1714 to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon" title="House of Bourbon">Bourbon</a> king <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a> militarily ended the Habsburg claim to the Spanish Crown, which became legal fact in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a>. Philip felt that he had been betrayed by the Catalan Courts, as it had initially sworn its loyalty to him when he had presided over it in 1701. In retaliation for the betrayal, the first Bourbon king introduced the <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">Nueva Planta decrees</a> that incorporated the territories of the Crown of Aragon, including Catalonia, as provinces under the Crown of Castile in 1716, terminating their separate institutions, laws and rights, within a united kingdom of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> During the second half of 18th century Catalonia started a successful process of <a href="/wiki/Proto-industrialization" title="Proto-industrialization">proto-industrialization</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Industrialisation.2C_Republic_and_autonomy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industrialisation,_Republic_and_autonomy">Industrialisation, Republic and autonomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Industrialisation, Republic and autonomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg/220px-Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg/330px-Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg/440px-Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2297" data-file-height="2353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cesar_Alvarez_Dumont_-_El_Gran_dia_de_Girona.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Third_Siege_of_Girona" title="Third Siege of Girona">Third Siege of Girona</a> (1809), <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> against Napoleon</div></div></div>
<p>At the beginning of the nineteenth century Catalonia was severely affected by the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>. In 1808 it was occupied by the French troops, the resistance against the occupation eventually developed into the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a>. The rejection to French dominion was institutionalized with the creation of "juntas" (councils) who, remaining loyal to the Bourbons, exercised the sovereignty and representation of the territory due to the disappearance of the old institutions. Napoleon took direct control of Catalonia to establish order, creating the Government of Catalonia under the rule of <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Augereau" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall Augereau">Marshall Augereau</a>, and making Catalan briefly an official language again. Between 1812 and 1814 Catalonia was annexed to France and organized as four <a href="/wiki/French_departments_of_Spain" title="French departments of Spain">départements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The French troops evacuated Catalan territory at the end of 1814. After the Bourbon restoration in Spain and the death of the abolutist king <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferdinand VII">Ferdinand VII</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlist_Wars" title="Carlist Wars">Carlist Wars</a> erupted against the new born <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberal state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Isabella II</a>. Catalonia was divided, the coast and most industrialized areas support liberalism, while many inland areas were in the hands of <a href="/wiki/Carlism" title="Carlism">Carlists</a>, as the last ones proposed to reestablish the intitutional systems suppressed in the Nueva Planta decrees in all the ancient realms of the Crown of Aragon.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Semana_tragica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Semana_tragica.jpg/220px-Semana_tragica.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Semana_tragica.jpg/330px-Semana_tragica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Semana_tragica.jpg/440px-Semana_tragica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1262" data-file-height="842" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Semana_tragica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Demonstration after the <a href="/wiki/Tragic_Week_(Catalonia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tragic Week (Catalonia)">Tragic Week</a>, 1909</div></div></div>
<p>In the second third of the 19th century, it became an industrial center. This process was boosted by, amongst other things, national <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ley_de_Relaciones_Comerciales_con_las_Antillas" class="extiw" title="es:Ley de Relaciones Comerciales con las Antillas">protectionist laws</a> (although the policy of the Spanish government during those times changed many times between free trade and protectionism) and the conditions of proto-industrialization of the prior two centuries of the Catalan urban areas and its countryside. Along the century, textile industry flourished in urban areas and in the countryside, usually in the form of <a href="/wiki/Company_towns" class="mw-redirect" title="Company towns">company towns</a>. To this day it remains one of the most industrialised areas of Spain. In 1832 it was inaugurated in Barcelona the factory Bonaplata, the first of the country which worked with <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a>. During those years, Barcelona was the focus of important revolutionary uprisings, called "bullangues", causing a difficult relation between many sectors of Catalan society and the central government and, in Catalonia, a <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republican</a> current began to develop; also, inevitably, many Catalans favored a more federal Spain. Meanwhile, the Catalan language saw a cultural renaissance (the <i><a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">Renaixença</a></i>) at popular and bourgeois level. After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/First_Spanish_Republic" title="First Spanish Republic">First Spanish Republic</a> and the restoration of the Bourbon dynasty (1874), Catalan nationalism grew in importance.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543,_Madrid,_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543%2C_Madrid%2C_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="514" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_102-11543,_Madrid,_Ausrufung_der_Zweiten_Spanischen_Republik.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a> on 14 April 1931 in Barcelona</div></div></div>
<p>The Anarchists had been active throughout the early 20th century, founding the <a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederación Nacional del Trabajo">CNT</a> trade union and achieving one of the first <a href="/wiki/Eight-hour_day" title="Eight-hour day">eight-hour workday</a> in Europe in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Growing resentment of conscription and of the military culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Tragic_Week_(Catalonia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tragic Week (Catalonia)">Tragic Week</a> in Barcelona in 1909. In the first third of the 20th century, Catalonia gained and lost varying degrees of autonomy several times. In 1914, the four Catalan provinces were authorized to create a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Catalonia" title="Commonwealth of Catalonia">Commonwealth</a> (<i>Mancomunitat</i>), without any legislative power or specific autonomy which carried out an ambitious program of modernization, but that was disbanded in 1925 by the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Primo_de_Rivera" title="Miguel Primo de Rivera">Primo de Rivera</a> (1923-1930). During the last steps of the Dictatorship, Barcelona celebrated the <a href="/wiki/1929_Barcelona_International_Exposition" title="1929 Barcelona International Exposition">1929 International Exposition</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-MonclúsFraga2006_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MonclúsFraga2006-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> while Spain started to suffer an economical crisis.
</p><p>After the fall of the dictator and a brief proclamation of the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Republic_(1931)" title="Catalan Republic (1931)">Catalan Republic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> it received its <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy_of_Catalonia_of_1932" title="Statute of Autonomy of Catalonia of 1932">first Statute of Autonomy</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a> (1931–1939), establishing an autonomous body, the Generalitat of Catalonia, which included a parliament, a government and a <a href="/wiki/Tribunal_de_Cassaci%C3%B3" title="Tribunal de Cassació">court of appeal</a>, and the left-wing independentist leader <a href="/wiki/Francesc_Maci%C3%A0" title="Francesc Macià">Francesc Macià</a> was elected its first president. The governments of the Republican Generalitat, led by the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Left_of_Catalonia" title="Republican Left of Catalonia">Republican Left of Catalonia</a> (ERC) members Francesc Macià (1931-1933) and <a href="/wiki/Llu%C3%ADs_Companys" title="Lluís Companys">Lluís Companys</a> (1933-1940) tried to implement an advanced social program, despite the internal difficulties. This period was marked by political unrest, the effects of the economic crisis and their social repercussions. The Statute was suspended in 1934, due to the <a href="/wiki/Events_of_6_October" title="Events of 6 October">Events of 6 October</a> in Barcelona, as a response<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> to the accession of right-wing Spanish nationalist party <a href="/wiki/CEDA" title="CEDA">CEDA</a> to the government of the Republic, considered close to <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
After the electoral victory of the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Front_(Spain)" title="Popular Front (Spain)">Popular Front</a> in February 1936, the Government of Catalonia was pardoned and the self-government restored.
</p>
<h3><span id="Spanish_Civil_War_.281936.E2.80.931939.29_and_Franco.27s_rule_.281939.E2.80.931975.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_Civil_War_(1936–1939)_and_Franco's_rule_(1939–1975)">Spanish Civil War (1936–1939) and Franco's rule (1939–1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Spanish Civil War (1936–1939) and Franco&#039;s rule (1939–1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_Catalonia" title="Revolutionary Catalonia">Revolutionary Catalonia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Catalonia" title="Francoist Catalonia">Francoist Catalonia</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:419px;max-width:419px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:190px;max-width:190px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_(3334194838).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg/188px-Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="188" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg/282px-Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg/376px-Strijdlustige_vrouw_-_Woman_ready_to_fight_%283334194838%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="731" data-file-height="566" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:225px;max-width:225px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona_bombing_(1938).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg/223px-Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="223" height="145" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg/335px-Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg/446px-Barcelona_bombing_%281938%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="1872" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Left: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Revolution_of_1936" title="Spanish Revolution of 1936">Spanish Revolution of 1936</a>. Right: <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Barcelona" title="Bombing of Barcelona">Bombing of Barcelona</a> (1938)</div></div></div></div>
<p>The defeat of the <a href="/wiki/July_1936_military_uprising_in_Barcelona" title="July 1936 military uprising in Barcelona">military rebellion against the Republican government in Barcelona</a> placed Catalonia firmly in the <a href="/wiki/Republican_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Republican faction (Spanish Civil War)">Republican side</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>. During the war, there were two rival powers in Catalonia: the de jure power of the Generalitat and the de facto power of the armed popular militias.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Violent confrontations between the workers' parties (<a href="/wiki/CNT-FAI" class="mw-redirect" title="CNT-FAI">CNT-FAI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Workers_Party_of_Marxist_Unification" class="mw-redirect" title="Workers Party of Marxist Unification">POUM</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Socialist_Party_of_Catalonia" title="Unified Socialist Party of Catalonia">PSUC</a>) culminated in the defeat of the first ones in 1937. The situation resolved itself progressively in favor of the Generalitat, but at the same time the Generalitat was partially losing its autonomous power within Republican Spain. In 1938 Franco's troops broke the Republican territory in two, isolating Catalonia from the rest of the Republic. The defeat of the Republican army in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Ebro" title="Battle of the Ebro">Battle of the Ebro</a> led in 1938 and 1939 to the occupation of Catalonia by Franco's forces.
</p><p>
The defeat of the Spanish Republic in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> brought to power the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>, whose first ten-year rule was particularly violent, autocratic, and repressive both in a political, cultural, social, and economical sense.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In Catalonia, any kind of public activities associated with <a href="/wiki/Catalan_nationalism" title="Catalan nationalism">Catalan nationalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liberalism" title="Liberalism">liberalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy" title="Democracy">democracy</a> or <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communism</a>, including the publication of books on those subjects or simply discussion of them in open meetings, was banned. </p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FrancoenReus.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FrancoenReus.jpg/220px-FrancoenReus.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FrancoenReus.jpg/330px-FrancoenReus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/FrancoenReus.jpg/440px-FrancoenReus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="870" data-file-height="590" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FrancoenReus.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> in <a href="/wiki/Reus" title="Reus">Reus</a>, 1940</div></div></div><p> Franco's regime banned the use of Catalan in government-run institutions and during public events, and also the Catalan institutions of self-government were abolished. The pro-Republic of Spain president of Catalonia, <a href="/wiki/Llu%C3%ADs_Companys" title="Lluís Companys">Lluís Companys</a>, was taken to Spain from his exile in the German-occupied France, and was tortured and executed in the <a href="/wiki/Montju%C3%AFc_Castle_(Barcelona)" title="Montjuïc Castle (Barcelona)">Montjuïc Castle</a> of Barcelona for the crime of 'military rebellion'.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During later stages of <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a>, certain folkloric and religious celebrations in Catalan resumed and were tolerated. Use of Catalan in the <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">mass media</a> had been forbidden, but was permitted from the early 1950s<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> in the theatre. Despite the ban during the first years and the difficulties of the next period, publishing in Catalan continued throughout his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The years after the war were extremely hard. Catalonia, like many other parts of Spain, had been devastated by the war. Recovery from the war damage was slow and made more difficult by the international trade embargo and the <a href="/wiki/Autarky" title="Autarky">autarkic</a> politics of Franco's regime. By the late 1950s the region had recovered its pre-war economic levels and in the 1960s was the second fastest growing economy in the world in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_miracle" title="Spanish miracle">Spanish miracle</a>. During this period there was a spectacular growth of industry and tourism in Catalonia that drew large numbers of workers to the region from across Spain and made the area around Barcelona into one of Europe's largest industrial metropolitan areas.
</p>
<h3><span id="Transition_and_democratic_period_.281975.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Transition_and_democratic_period_(1975–present)">Transition and democratic period (1975–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Transition and democratic period (1975–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_(Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992)_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg/200px-Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg/300px-Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg/400px-Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_%28Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992%29_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="785" data-file-height="927" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barcelona_AUGUST_1992_the_Olympic_Games_(Juegos_Ol%C3%ADmpicos_de_Barcelona_1992)_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Olympic flame in the <a href="/wiki/Estadi_Ol%C3%ADmpic_Llu%C3%ADs_Companys" title="Estadi Olímpic Lluís Companys">Olympic Stadium Lluís Companys</a> of <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> during the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a></div></div></div>
<p>After Franco's death in 1975, Catalonia voted for the adoption of a democratic Spanish Constitution in 1978, in which Catalonia recovered political and cultural autonomy, restoring the Generalitat (exiled since the end of the Civil War in 1939) in 1977 and adopting a <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy_of_Catalonia_of_1979" title="Statute of Autonomy of Catalonia of 1979">new Statute of Autonomy</a> in 1979. <a href="/wiki/1980_Catalan_regional_election" title="1980 Catalan regional election">First election</a> to the Parliament of Catalonia under this Statute gave the Catalan presidency to <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Pujol" title="Jordi Pujol">Jordi Pujol</a>, a position he would hold until 2003. During this time, he also led <a href="/wiki/Convergence_and_Unity" class="mw-redirect" title="Convergence and Unity">Convergència i Unió</a> (CiU), a center-right Catalan nationalist electoral coalition. Throughout the 1980s and 1990s, the institutions of Catalan autonomy continued to develop, among them an autonomous police force (<i><a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d&#39;Esquadra">Mossos d'Esquadra</a></i>, in 1983),<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and the broadcasting network <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3_de_Catalunya" title="Televisió de Catalunya">Televisió de Catalunya</a> and its first channel <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Catalonia)" title="TV3 (Catalonia)">TV3</a>, created in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Today, Catalonia is one of the most economically dynamic communities of Spain. The Catalan capital and largest city, Barcelona, is a major international cultural centre and a major tourist destination. In 1992, <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">Barcelona hosted</a> the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Olympic Games</a>.
</p><p>In November 2003, elections to the Parliament of Catalonia gave the government to a left-wing catalanist coalition formed by the <a href="/wiki/Socialists%27_Party_of_Catalonia" title="Socialists&#39; Party of Catalonia">Socialists' Party of Catalonia</a> (PSC-PSOE), <a href="/wiki/Republican_Left_of_Catalonia" title="Republican Left of Catalonia">Republican Left of Catalonia</a> (ERC) and <a href="/wiki/Initiative_for_Catalonia_Greens" title="Initiative for Catalonia Greens">Initiative for Catalonia Greens</a> (ICV), and the socialist <a href="/wiki/Pasqual_Maragall" title="Pasqual Maragall">Pasqual Maragall</a> was appointed President. The new government redacted a <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Autonomy_of_Catalonia" title="Statute of Autonomy of Catalonia">new version of the Statute of Autonomy</a>, which consolidated and extended certain aspects of self-government.
</p><p>The new Statute of Autonomy of Catalonia, approved after a referendum in 2006, was contested by important sectors of the Spanish society, especially by the conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a>, which sent the law to the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Spain" title="Constitutional Court of Spain">Constitutional Court of Spain</a>. In 2010, the Court declared non valid some of the articles that established an autonomous Catalan system of Justice, better aspects of the financing, a new territorial division, the status of Catalan language or the symbolical declaration of Catalonia as a nation.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> This decision was severely contested by large sectors of Catalan society, which increased the demands of independence.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Independence movement</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Catalan_independence_movement" title="Catalan independence movement">Catalan independence movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Spanish_constitutional_crisis" title="2017–18 Spanish constitutional crisis">2017–18 Spanish constitutional crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Puigdemont,_%22Ciutadans_de_Catalunya,_v%C3%A9nen_hores_en_qu%C3%A8_a_tots_ens_pertocar%C3%A0_de_mantenir_el_pols_del_nostre_pa%C3%ADs%22_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/President_Puigdemont%2C_%22Ciutadans_de_Catalunya%2C_v%C3%A9nen_hores_en_qu%C3%A8_a_tots_ens_pertocar%C3%A0_de_mantenir_el_pols_del_nostre_pa%C3%ADs%22_02.jpg/220px-President_Puigdemont%2C_%22Ciutadans_de_Catalunya%2C_v%C3%A9nen_hores_en_qu%C3%A8_a_tots_ens_pertocar%C3%A0_de_mantenir_el_pols_del_nostre_pa%C3%ADs%22_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/President_Puigdemont%2C_%22Ciutadans_de_Catalunya%2C_v%C3%A9nen_hores_en_qu%C3%A8_a_tots_ens_pertocar%C3%A0_de_mantenir_el_pols_del_nostre_pa%C3%ADs%22_02.jpg/330px-President_Puigdemont%2C_%22Ciutadans_de_Catalunya%2C_v%C3%A9nen_hores_en_qu%C3%A8_a_tots_ens_pertocar%C3%A0_de_mantenir_el_pols_del_nostre_pa%C3%ADs%22_02.jpg
