<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a>, Catalan was excluded from the public education system and all other official use, so that for example families were not allowed to officially register children with Catalan names.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Although never completely banned, Catalan language publishing was severely restricted during the early 1940s, with only religious texts and small-run self-published texts being released. Some books were published clandestinely or circumvented the restrictions by showing publishing dates prior to 1936.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> This policy was changed in 1946, when restricted publishing in Catalan resumed.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Rural–urban migration originating in other parts of Spain also reduced the social use of Catalan in urban areas and increased the use of Spanish. Lately, a similar <a href="/wiki/Sociolinguistic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sociolinguistic">sociolinguistic</a> phenomenon has occurred with foreign immigration. Catalan cultural activity increased in the 1960s and Catalan classes began thanks to the initiative of associations such as <a href="/wiki/%C3%92mnium_Cultural" title="Òmnium Cultural">Òmnium Cultural</a>.
</p><p>After the end of Francoist Spain, the newly established self-governing democratic institutions in Catalonia embarked on a long-term <a href="/wiki/Language_policy" title="Language policy">language policy</a> to recover the use of Catalan<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> and has, since 1983, enforced laws which attempt to protect and extend the use of Catalan. This policy, known as the "linguistic normalisation" (<i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">normalització lingüística</i> in Catalan, <i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">normalización lingüística</i> in Spanish) has been supported by the vast majority of Catalan political parties through the last thirty years. Some groups consider these efforts a way to discourage the use of Spanish,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> whereas some others, including the Catalan government<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and the European Union<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> consider the policies respectful,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> or even as an example which "should be disseminated throughout the Union".<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg/220px-Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="286" data-file-height="255" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fragment of the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">Greuges de Guirard Isarn</i> (<abbr title="circa">c.</abbr><span style="white-space:nowrap;">&#8201;1080</span>–1095), one of the earliest texts written almost completely in Catalan,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVeny19979–18_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVeny19979–18-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (October 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="A complete citation is needed (October 2018)">full citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> predating the famous <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Homilies_d%27Organy%C3%A0" title="Homilies d&#39;Organyà">Homilies d'Organyà</a></i> by a century</div></div></div><p>Today, Catalan is the main language of the Catalan autonomous government and the other public institutions that fall under its jurisdiction. Basic public education is given basically in Catalan, but also there are some hours per week of Spanish medium instruction. Businesses are required to display all information (e.g. menus, posters) at least in Catalan, under penalty of fines. There is no obligation to display this information in either Occitan or Spanish, although there is no restriction on doing so in these or other languages. The use of fines was introduced in a 1997 linguistic law<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> that aims to increase the public use of Catalan and defend the rights of Catalan speakers. In the other hand, the constitution of Spain obligates every citizen to know Spanish.
</p><p>The law ensures that both Catalan and Spanish – being official languages – can be used by the citizens without prejudice in all public and private activities,.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The Generalitat uses Catalan in its communications and notifications addressed to the general population, but citizens can also receive information from the Generalitat in Spanish if they so desire.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Debates in the Catalan Parliament take place almost exclusively in Catalan and the <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Catalonia)" title="TV3 (Catalonia)">Catalan public television</a> broadcasts programs basically in Catalan.
</p><p>Due to the <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Spain" title="Immigration to Spain">intense immigration</a> which Spain in general and Catalonia in particular experienced in the first decade of the 21st century, many foreign languages are spoken in various cultural communities in Catalonia, of which <a href="/wiki/Riff_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Riff language">Rif</a>-<a href="/wiki/Berber_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber language">Berber</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Arabic" title="Moroccan Arabic">Moroccan Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romanian_language" title="Romanian language">Romanian</a><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> are the most common ones.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Catalonia, there is a high social and political consensus on the language policies favoring Catalan, also among Spanish speakers and speakers of other languages.<sup id="cite_ref-presencia.cat_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presencia.cat-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (September 2019)">needs update</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> However, some of these policies have been criticised for trying to promote Catalan by imposing fines on businesses. For example, following the passage of the law on Catalan cinema in March 2010, which established that half of the movies shown in Catalan cinemas had to be in Catalan, a general strike of 75% of the cinemas took place.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> The Catalan government gave in and dropped the clause that forced 50% of the movies to be dubbed or subtitled in Catalan before the law came to effect.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, organisations such as <a href="/wiki/Plataforma_per_la_Llengua" title="Plataforma per la Llengua">Plataforma per la Llengua</a> reported different violations of the linguistic rights of the Catalan speakers in Catalonia and the other Catalan-speaking territories in Spain, most of them caused by the institutions of the Spanish government in these territories.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Catalan language policy has been challenged by some political parties in the Catalan Parliament. <a href="/wiki/Citizens_-_Party_of_the_Citizenry" class="mw-redirect" title="Citizens - Party of the Citizenry">Citizens</a>, currently the main opposition party, has been one of the most consistent critics of the Catalan language policy within Catalonia. The Catalan branch of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> has a more ambiguous position on the issue: on one hand, it demands a bilingual Catalan–Spanish education and a more balanced language policy that would defend Catalan without favoring it over Spanish,<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> whereas on the other hand, a few local PP politicians have supported in their municipalities measures privileging Catalan over Spanish<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and it has defended some aspects of the official language policies, sometimes against the positions of its colleagues from other parts of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Art and architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Art of Catalonia">Art of Catalonia</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:288px;max-width:288px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Joan_Miro,_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg/140px-Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg/210px-Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg/280px-Portrait_of_Joan_Miro%2C_Barcelona_1935_June_13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1191" data-file-height="1516" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Gaud%C3%AD_(1878).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg/140px-Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg/210px-Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg/280px-Gaud%C3%AD_%281878%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1375" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Left: <a href="/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3" title="Joan Miró">Joan Miró</a>. Right: <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Gaud%C3%AD" title="Antoni Gaudí">Antoni Gaudí</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Catalonia has given to the world many important figures in the area of the art. Catalan painters internationally known are, among others, <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">Salvador Dalí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3" title="Joan Miró">Joan Miró</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antoni_T%C3%A0pies" title="Antoni Tàpies">Antoni Tàpies</a>. Closely linked with the Catalan pictorial atmosphere, <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Picasso" title="Pablo Picasso">Pablo Picasso</a> lived in Barcelona during his youth, training them as an artist and creating the movement of <a href="/wiki/Cubism" title="Cubism">cubism</a>. Other important artists are <a href="/wiki/Claudi_Lorenzale" title="Claudi Lorenzale">Claudi Lorenzale</a> for the medieval <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a> that marked the artistic Renaixença, <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A0_Fortuny" title="Marià Fortuny">Marià Fortuny</a> for the Romanticism and Catalan Orientalism of the nineteenth century, <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Casas" title="Ramon Casas">Ramon Casas</a> or <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Rusi%C3%B1ol" title="Santiago Rusiñol">Santiago Rusiñol</a>, main representatives of the pictorial current of Catalan modernism from the end of the nineteenth century to the beginning of the twentieth century, <a href="/wiki/Josep_Maria_Sert" title="Josep Maria Sert">Josep Maria Sert</a> for early 20th-century Noucentisme, or <a href="/wiki/Josep_Maria_Subirachs" title="Josep Maria Subirachs">Josep Maria Subirachs</a> for expressionist or abstract sculpture and painting of the late twentieth century.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:508px;max-width:508px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:262px;max-width:262px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg/260px-MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg/390px-MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg/520px-MNAC_2010-08-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3039" data-file-height="2106" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg/240px-20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="180" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg/360px-20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg/480px-20061227-Figueres_Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD_MQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Left: <a href="/wiki/Museu_Nacional_d%27Art_de_Catalunya" title="Museu Nacional d&#39;Art de Catalunya">Museu Nacional d'Art de Catalunya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. Right: <a href="/wiki/Dal%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Dalí">Dalí</a> Museum, <a href="/wiki/Figueres" title="Figueres">Figueres</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>The most important painting museums of Catalonia are the <a href="/wiki/Teatre-Museu_Dal%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Teatre-Museu Dalí">Teatre-Museu Dalí</a> in Figueres, the <a href="/wiki/National_Art_Museum_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="National Art Museum of Catalonia">National Art Museum of Catalonia</a> (MNAC), <a href="/wiki/Picasso_Museum,_Barcelona" class="mw-redirect" title="Picasso Museum, Barcelona">Picasso Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fundaci%C3%B3_Antoni_T%C3%A0pies" title="Fundació Antoni Tàpies">Fundació Antoni Tàpies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Mir%C3%B3_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Joan Miró Foundation">Joan Miró Foundation</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Museum_of_Contemporary_Art" title="Barcelona Museum of Contemporary Art">Barcelona Museum of Contemporary Art</a> (MACBA), the <a href="/wiki/Centre_de_Cultura_Contempor%C3%A0nia_de_Barcelona" title="Centre de Cultura Contemporània de Barcelona">Centre of Contemporary Culture of Barcelona</a> (CCCB) and the <a href="/wiki/CaixaForum_Barcelona" title="CaixaForum Barcelona">CaixaForum</a>.
</p><p>In the field of architecture were developed and adapted to Catalonia different artistic styles prevalent in Europe, leaving footprints in many churches, monasteries and cathedrals, of <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> (the best examples of which are located in the northern half of the territory) and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic style">Gothic styles</a>. The Gothic developed in Barcelona and its area of influence is known as <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Gothic" title="Catalan Gothic">Catalan Gothic</a>, with some particular characteristics. The church of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Mar,_Barcelona" title="Santa Maria del Mar, Barcelona">Santa Maria del Mar</a> is an example of this kind of style. During the Middle Ages, many fortified castles were built by feudal nobles to mark their powers.
</p><p>There are some examples of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance</a> (such as the Palau de la Generalitat), <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical architectures</a>. In the late nineteenth century <a href="/wiki/Modernisme" title="Modernisme">Modernism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>) appeared as the national art. The world-renowned Catalan architects of this style are <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Gaud%C3%AD" title="Antoni Gaudí">Antoni Gaudí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Llu%C3%ADs_Dom%C3%A8nech_i_Montaner" title="Lluís Domènech i Montaner">Lluís Domènech i Montaner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josep_Puig_i_Cadafalch" title="Josep Puig i Cadafalch">Josep Puig i Cadafalch</a>. Thanks to the urban expansion of Barcelona during the last decades of the century and the first ones of the next, many buildings of the <a href="/wiki/Eixample" title="Eixample">Eixample</a> are modernists. In the field of <a href="/wiki/Architectural_rationalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Architectural rationalism">architectural rationalism</a>, which turned especially relevant in Catalonia during the Republican era (1931-1939) highlighting <a href="/wiki/Josep_Llu%C3%ADs_Sert" title="Josep Lluís Sert">Josep Lluís Sert</a> and Josep Torres i Clavé, members of the <a href="/wiki/GATCPAC" class="mw-redirect" title="GATCPAC">GATCPAC</a> and, in contemporany architecture, <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Bofill" title="Ricardo Bofill">Ricardo Bofill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enric_Miralles" title="Enric Miralles">Enric Miralles</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Monuments_and_World_Heritage_Sites">Monuments and World Heritage Sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Monuments and World Heritage Sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg/220px-Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg/330px-Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg/440px-Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="398" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sant-climent-exterior-boi04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Medieval church of <a href="/wiki/Sant_Climent_de_Ta%C3%BCll" class="mw-redirect" title="Sant Climent de Taüll">Sant Climent de Taüll</a>, located at the foothills of the Pyrenees, in the province of Lleida</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg/220px-%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="325" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg/330px-%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg/440px-%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2774" data-file-height="4099" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%CE%A3%CE%B1%CE%B3%CF%81%CE%AC%CE%B4%CE%B1_%CE%A6%CE%B1%CE%BC%CE%AF%CE%BB%CE%B9%CE%B1_2941.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sagrada_Fam%C3%ADlia" title="Sagrada Família">Sagrada Família</a>, Barcelona</div></div></div>
<p>There are several <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> in Catalonia:
</p>
<ul><li>Archaeological Ensemble of <a href="/wiki/Tarraco" title="Tarraco">Tarraco</a>, Tarragona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Catalan_Romanesque_Churches_of_the_Vall_de_Bo%C3%AD" title="Catalan Romanesque Churches of the Vall de Boí">Catalan Romanesque Churches of the Vall de Boí</a>, Lleida province</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Poblet_Monastery" title="Poblet Monastery">Poblet Monastery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poblet" class="mw-redirect" title="Poblet">Poblet</a>, Tarragona province</li>
<li>Works of <a href="/wiki/Llu%C3%ADs_Dom%C3%A8nech_i_Montaner" title="Lluís Domènech i Montaner">Lluís Domènech i Montaner</a>:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Palau_de_la_M%C3%BAsica_Catalana" title="Palau de la Música Catalana">Palau de la Música Catalana</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hospital_de_Sant_Pau" title="Hospital de Sant Pau">Hospital de Sant Pau</a>, Barcelona</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Works_of_Antoni_Gaud%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Works of Antoni Gaudí">Works of Antoni Gaudí</a>:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Sagrada_Fam%C3%ADlia" title="Sagrada Família">Sagrada Família</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Park_Guell" class="mw-redirect" title="Park Guell">Parc Güell</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palau_G%C3%BCell" title="Palau Güell">Palau Güell</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Mil%C3%A0" title="Casa Milà">Casa Milà</a> (La Pedrera), Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Vicens" title="Casa Vicens">Casa Vicens</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Casa_Batll%C3%B3" title="Casa Batlló">Casa Batlló</a>, Barcelona</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Col%C3%B2nia_G%C3%BCell" title="Church of Colònia Güell">Church of Colònia Güell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Coloma_de_Cervell%C3%B3" title="Santa Coloma de Cervelló">Santa Coloma de Cervelló</a>, Barcelona province</li></ul></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Catalonia">Literature of Catalonia</a></div>
<p>Literary use of the Catalan language is considered to have started with the religious text known as <a href="/wiki/Homilies_d%27Organy%C3%A0" title="Homilies d&#39;Organyà">Homilies d'Organyà</a>, written either in late 11th or early 12th century.
</p><p>There are two historical moments of splendor of Catalan literature. The first begins with the historiography chronicles of the 13th century (chronicles written between the thirteenth and fourteenth centuries narrating the deeds of the monarchs and leading figures of the Crown of Aragon) and the subsequent Golden Age of the 14th and 15th centuries. After that period, between the 16th and 19th centuries the Romantic <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a> defined this era as the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Decad%C3%A8ncia" class="mw-redirect" title="Decadència">Decadència</a></i>, considered as the "decadent" period in Catalan literature because of a general falling into disuse of the vernacular language in cultural contexts and lack of patronage among the nobility.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodoreda.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Rodoreda.jpg/130px-Rodoreda.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Rodoreda.jpg/195px-Rodoreda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Rodoreda.jpg/260px-Rodoreda.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rodoreda.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Merc%C3%A8_Rodoreda" title="Mercè Rodoreda">Mercè Rodoreda</a></div></div></div><p>
The second moment of splendor began in the 19th century with the cultural and political <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">Renaixença</a></i> (Renaissance) represented by writers and poets such as <a href="/wiki/Jacint_Verdaguer" title="Jacint Verdaguer">Jacint Verdaguer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narc%C3%ADs_Oller" title="Narcís Oller">Narcís Oller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Maragall" title="Joan Maragall">Joan Maragall</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C3%80ngel_Guimer%C3%A0" title="Àngel Guimerà">Àngel Guimerà</a>. During the 20th century were developed the avant-garde movements initiated by the Generation of '14 (called <a href="/wiki/Noucentisme" title="Noucentisme">Noucentisme</a> in Catalonia), represented by <a href="/wiki/Eugeni_d%27Ors" title="Eugeni d&#39;Ors">Eugeni d'Ors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Salvat-Papasseit" title="Joan Salvat-Papasseit">Joan Salvat-Papasseit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josep_Carner" title="Josep Carner">Josep Carner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carles_Riba" title="Carles Riba">Carles Riba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josep_Vicen%C3%A7_Foix_i_Mas" class="mw-redirect" title="Josep Vicenç Foix i Mas">J.V. Foix</a> and others. During the dictatorship of Primo de Rivera, the Civil War (<a href="/wiki/Generation_of_%2736" title="Generation of &#39;36">Generation of '36</a>) and the Francoist period, Catalan literature is maintained despite the repression against the Catalan language, being often produced in exile. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg/130px-Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg/195px-Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/85/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg 2x" data-file-width="197" data-file-height="305" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute" title="Ana María Matute">Ana María Matute</a></div></div></div><p> The most outstanding authors of this period are <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Espriu" title="Salvador Espriu">Salvador Espriu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josep_Pla" title="Josep Pla">Josep Pla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Josep_Maria_de_Sagarra" title="Josep Maria de Sagarra">Josep Maria de Sagarra</a> (the latter three being considered as the main responsible of the renewal of Catalan prose), <a href="/wiki/Merc%C3%A8_Rodoreda" title="Mercè Rodoreda">Mercè Rodoreda</a>, Joan Oliver Sallarès or "<a href="/wiki/Pere_Quart" class="mw-redirect" title="Pere Quart">Pere Quart</a>", <a href="/wiki/Pere_Calders" title="Pere Calders">Pere Calders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ferrater" title="Gabriel Ferrater">Gabriel Ferrater</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Pedrolo" title="Manuel de Pedrolo">Manuel de Pedrolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%AD_Bartra" title="Agustí Bartra">Agustí Bartra</a> or <a href="/wiki/Miquel_Mart%C3%AD_i_Pol" title="Miquel Martí i Pol">Miquel Martí i Pol</a>. In addition, several foreign writers who fought in the framework of the <a href="/wiki/International_Brigades" title="International Brigades">International Brigades</a> then recount their experiences of fighting in their works, historical or fictional, with for example <i><a href="/wiki/Homage_to_Catalonia" title="Homage to Catalonia">Homage to Catalonia</a></i> of the British <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a> in 1938 or <i lang="fr" title="French language text"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Le_Palace_(Claude_Simon)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Le Palace (Claude Simon) (page does not exist)">Le Palace</a></i> in 1962 and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Georgics_(Claude_Simon)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Georgics (Claude Simon) (page does not exist)">The Georgics</a></i> in 1981 by Frenchman <a href="/wiki/Claude_Simon" title="Claude Simon">Claude Simon</a>.
</p><p>After the transition to democracy (1975–1978) and the restoration of the Generalitat (1977), literary life and the editorial market have returned to normality and literary production in Catalan is being bolstered with a number of language policies intended to protect Catalan culture. Besides the aforementioned authors, other relevant 20th-century writers of the Francoist and democracy periods include <a href="/wiki/Joan_Brossa" title="Joan Brossa">Joan Brossa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%AD_Bartra" title="Agustí Bartra">Agustí Bartra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Pedrolo" title="Manuel de Pedrolo">Manuel de Pedrolo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pere_Calders" title="Pere Calders">Pere Calders</a> or <a href="/wiki/Quim_Monz%C3%B3" title="Quim Monzó">Quim Monzó</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ana_Mar%C3%ADa_Matute" title="Ana María Matute">Ana María Matute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Gil_de_Biedma" title="Jaime Gil de Biedma">Jaime Gil de Biedma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manuel_V%C3%A1zquez_Montalb%C3%A1n" title="Manuel Vázquez Montalbán">Manuel Vázquez Montalbán</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Goytisolo" title="Juan Goytisolo">Juan Goytisolo</a> are among the most prominent Catalan writers in the Spanish language since the democratic restoration in Spain.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_public_holidays">Festivals and public holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Festivals and public holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Traditions_of_Catalonia" title="Traditions of Catalonia">Traditions of Catalonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg/220px-4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg/330px-4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/52/4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="426" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:4_de_9_amb_folre_i_pilar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Castell 4 de 9 amb folre i pilar by Colla Vella de Valls</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Castell" title="Castell">Castells</a> are one of the main manifestations of Catalan popular culture. The activity consists in constructing human towers by competing <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">colles castelleres</i> (teams). This practice originated in <a href="/wiki/Valls" title="Valls">Valls</a>, on the region of the Camp de Tarragona, during the 18th century, and later it was extended along the next two centuries to the rest of the territory. The tradition of <a href="/wiki/Castell" title="Castell">els Castells i els Castellers</a> was declared Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 2010.
</p><p>In the greater celebrations other elements of the Catalan popular culture are usually present: the parades of <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Gegants_i_capgrossos" class="mw-redirect" title="Gegants i capgrossos">gegants</a></i> (giants) and <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Correfoc" title="Correfoc">correfocs</a></i> of devils and firecrackers. Another traditional celebration in Catalonia is <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Patum_de_Berga" title="Patum de Berga">La Patum de Berga</a></i>, declared Masterpiece of the Oral and Intangible Heritage of Humanity by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> on 25 November 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG/220px-Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG/330px-Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG/440px-Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2640" data-file-height="1540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Festa_major_de_la_Seu_d%27Urgell.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Gigantes_y_cabezudos" title="Gigantes y cabezudos">Gegants i capgrossos</a></i> during the festa major of <a href="/wiki/La_Seu_d%27Urgell" title="La Seu d&#39;Urgell">La Seu d'Urgell</a></div></div></div>
<p>There are some local <a href="/wiki/Christmas_traditions" title="Christmas traditions">Christmas traditions</a>; one of them is the popular figure of the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Ti%C3%B3_de_Nadal" title="Tió de Nadal">Tió de Nadal</a></i>, consisting in a hollow log which after few days taking care of it, during <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Christmas Day">Christmas Day</a> or on <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Eve" title="Christmas Eve">Christmas Eve</a> one orders it to defecate presents and, in order to make this, children beats the tió with sticks, while they singing various traditional songs. Another custom is to make a <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">pessebre</i> (Nativity scene), and usually includes the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Caganer" title="Caganer">caganer</a></i>, a figurine depicted in the act of defecation.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to traditional local Catalan culture, traditions from other parts of Spain can be found as a result of migration from other regions, for instance the celebration of the Andalusian <i lang="es" title="Spanish language text"><a href="/wiki/Seville_Fair" title="Seville Fair">Feria de Abril</a></i> in Catalonia.
</p><p>On 28 July 2010, second only after the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ban_on_bullfighting_in_Catalonia" title="Ban on bullfighting in Catalonia">Catalonia became another Spanish territory to forbid bullfighting</a>. The ban, which went into effect on 1 January 2012, had originated in a popular petition supported by over 180,000 signatures.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_dance">Music and dance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Music and dance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Catalonia" title="Music of Catalonia">Music of Catalonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sardanes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Sardanes.jpg/220px-Sardanes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Sardanes.jpg/330px-Sardanes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Sardanes.jpg/440px-Sardanes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sardanes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sardana" title="Sardana">Sardana</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sardana" title="Sardana">sardana</a> is considered to be the most characteristic Catalan folk dance, interpreted to the rhythm of <a href="/wiki/Tambori" title="Tambori">tamborí</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tible" class="mw-redirect" title="Tible">tible</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tenora" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenora">tenora</a> (from the oboe family), <a href="/wiki/Trumpet" title="Trumpet">trumpet</a>, trombó (<a href="/wiki/Trombone" title="Trombone">trombone</a>), fiscorn (family of bugles) and contrabaix with three strings played by a <a href="/wiki/Cobla" title="Cobla">cobla</a>, and are danced in a circle dance. Other tunes and dances of the traditional music are the contrapàs (obsolete today), <a href="/wiki/Ball_de_bastons" title="Ball de bastons">ball de bastons</a> (the "dance of sticks"), the moixiganga, the goigs (popular songs), the <a href="/wiki/Galop" title="Galop">galops</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Jota_(music)" title="Jota (music)">jota</a> in the southern part. The <a href="/wiki/Habanera_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Habanera (music)">havaneres</a> are characteristic in some marine localities of the Costa Brava, especially during the summer months when these songs are sung outdoors accompanied by a <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">cremat</i> of burned rum.
</p><p>Art music was first developed, up to the nineteenth century and, as in much of Europe, in a liturgical setting, particularly marked by the Escolania de Montserrat. The main Western musical trends have marked these productions, medieval monodies or polyphonies, with the work of <a href="/wiki/Abbot_Oliba" title="Abbot Oliba">Abbot Oliba</a> in the eleventh century or the compilation <a href="/wiki/Llibre_Vermell_de_Montserrat" title="Llibre Vermell de Montserrat">Llibre Vermell de Montserrat</a> ("Red Book of Montserrat") from the fourteenth century. Through the Renaissance there were authors such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pere_Albert_Vila&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pere Albert Vila (page does not exist)">Pere Albert Vila</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Brudieu" title="Joan Brudieu">Joan Brudieu</a> or the two <a href="/wiki/Mateu_Fletxa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mateu Fletxa">Mateu Fletxa</a> ("The Old" and "The Young"). Baroque had composers like <a href="/wiki/Joan_Cererols" title="Joan Cererols">Joan Cererols</a>. The Romantic music was represented by composers such as <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Sor" title="Fernando Sor">Fernando Sor</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Josep_Anselm_Clav%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Josep Anselm Clavé (page does not exist)">Josep Anselm Clavé</a> (father of choir movement in Catalonia and responsible of the music folk reviving) or <a href="/wiki/Felip_Pedrell" title="Felip Pedrell">Felip Pedrell</a>.
</p><p>Modernisme also expressed in musical terms from the end of the 19th century onwards, mixing folkloric and post-romantic influences, through the works of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Alb%C3%A9niz" title="Isaac Albéniz">Isaac Albéniz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Enric_Granados" class="mw-redirect" title="Enric Granados">Enric Granados</a>. The avant-garde spirit initiated by the modernists is prolonged throughout the twentieth century, thanks to the activities of the <a href="/wiki/Orfe%C3%B3_Catal%C3%A0" title="Orfeó Català">Orfeó Català</a>, a choral society founded in 1891, with its monumental concert hall, the <a href="/wiki/Palau_de_la_M%C3%BAsica_Catalana" title="Palau de la Música Catalana">Palau de la Música Catalana</a> in Catalan, built by Lluís Domènech i Montaner from 1905 to 1908, the <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Symphony_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona Symphony Orchestra">Barcelona Symphony Orchestra</a> created in 1944 and composers, conductors and musicians engaged against the Francoism like <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gerhard" title="Robert Gerhard">Robert Gerhard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eduard_Toldr%C3%A0" title="Eduard Toldrà">Eduard Toldrà</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pau_Casals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pau Casals">Pau Casals</a>.
</p><p>Performances of <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">opera</a>, mostly imported from Italy, began in the 18th century, but some native operas were written as well, including the ones by <a href="/wiki/Dom%C3%A8nec_Terradellas" title="Domènec Terradellas">Domènec Terradellas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carles_Baguer" class="mw-redirect" title="Carles Baguer">Carles Baguer</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ramon_Carles&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ramon Carles (page does not exist)">Ramon Carles</a>, Isaac Albéniz and Enric Granados. The Barcelona main opera house, <a href="/wiki/Gran_Teatre_del_Liceu" class="mw-redirect" title="Gran Teatre del Liceu">Gran Teatre del Liceu</a> (opened in 1847), remains one of the most important in Spain, hosting one of the most prestigious music schools in Barcelona, the <a href="/wiki/Conservatori_Superior_de_M%C3%BAsica_del_Liceu" title="Conservatori Superior de Música del Liceu">Conservatori Superior de Música del Liceu</a>. Several lyrical artists trained by this institution gained international renown during the 20th century, such as <a href="/wiki/Victoria_de_los_%C3%81ngeles" title="Victoria de los Ángeles">Victoria de los Ángeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Caball%C3%A9" title="Montserrat Caballé">Montserrat Caballé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giacomo_Aragall" title="Giacomo Aragall">Giacomo Aragall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josep_Carreras" class="mw-redirect" title="Josep Carreras">Josep Carreras</a>.
</p><p>Cellist <a href="/wiki/Pau_Casals" class="mw-redirect" title="Pau Casals">Pau Casals</a> is admired as an outstanding player. Other popular musical styles were born in the second half of the 20th century such as <a href="/wiki/Nova_Can%C3%A7%C3%B3" title="Nova Cançó">Nova Cançó</a> from the 1960s with <a href="/wiki/Llu%C3%ADs_Llach" title="Lluís Llach">Lluís Llach</a> and the group <a href="/wiki/Els_Setze_Jutges" title="Els Setze Jutges">Els Setze Jutges</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_rumba" title="Catalan rumba">Catalan rumba</a> in the 1960s with <a href="/wiki/Peret" title="Peret">Peret</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan Rock">Catalan Rock</a> from the late 1970s with <a href="/w/index.php?title=La_Banda_Trapera_del_R%C3%ADo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="La Banda Trapera del Río (page does not exist)">La Banda Trapera del Río</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decibelios&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Decibelios (page does not exist)">Decibelios</a> for Punk Rock, <a href="/wiki/Sau_(band)" title="Sau (band)">Sau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Els_Pets" title="Els Pets">Els Pets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sopa_de_Cabra" title="Sopa de Cabra">Sopa de Cabra</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lax%27n%27Busto" title="Lax&#39;n&#39;Busto">Lax'n'Busto</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pop_Rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop Rock">Pop Rock</a> or <a href="/wiki/Sangtra%C3%AFt" title="Sangtraït">Sangtraït</a> for hard rock, electropop since the 1990s with <a href="/wiki/OBK" title="OBK">OBK</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indie_pop" title="Indie pop">indie pop</a> from the 1990s.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_cinema">Media and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Media and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Cinema of Catalonia">Cinema of Catalonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TVC.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TVC.svg/220px-TVC.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TVC.svg/330px-TVC.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/TVC.svg/440px-TVC.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="191" data-file-height="96" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TVC.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of Televisió de Catalunya</div></div></div>
<p>Catalonia is the autonomous community, along with Madrid, that has the most media (TV, Magazines, Newspapers etc.). In Catalonia there is a wide variety of local and comarcal media. With the restoration of democracy, many newspapers and magazines, until then in the hands of the Franco government, were recovered in order to convert them into free and democratic media, while local radios and televisions were implemented.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3_de_Catalunya" title="Televisió de Catalunya">Televisió de Catalunya</a>, which broadcasts entirely in the Catalan language, is the main Catalan public TV. It has five channels: <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Catalonia)" title="TV3 (Catalonia)">TV3</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_33" title="El 33">El 33</a>/<a href="/wiki/Super3" title="Super3">Super3</a>, <a href="/wiki/3/24" title="3/24">3/24</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esport3" title="Esport3">Esport3</a> and <a href="/wiki/TV3CAT" title="TV3CAT">TV3CAT</a>. In 2018, TV3 became the first television channel to be the most viewed one for nine consecutive years in Catalonia.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> State televisions that broadcast in Catalonia in Spanish language include <a href="/wiki/Televisi%C3%B3n_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Televisión Española">Televisión Española</a> (with few emissions in Catalan), <a href="/wiki/Antena_3_(Spain)" title="Antena 3 (Spain)">Antena 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuatro_(TV_channel)" title="Cuatro (TV channel)">Cuatro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecinco" title="Telecinco">Telecinco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/La_Sexta" class="mw-redirect" title="La Sexta">La Sexta</a>. Other smaller Catalan television channels include; <a href="/wiki/8TV_(Catalonia)" title="8TV (Catalonia)">8TV</a> (owned by Grup Godó), <a href="/w/index.php?title=El_Punt_Avui_TV&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="El Punt Avui TV (page does not exist)">El Punt Avui TV</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_Punt_Avui_TV" class="extiw" title="ca:El Punt Avui TV">ca</a>&#93;</span>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona_media" title="FC Barcelona media">Barça TV</a> and the local televisions, the greatest exponent of which is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Betev%C3%A9&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Betevé (page does not exist)">betevé</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://ca.wikipedia.org/wiki/betev%C3%A9" class="extiw" title="ca:betevé">ca</a>&#93;</span>, the TV channel of Barcelona, which also broadcasts in Catalan.
</p><p>The two main Catalan newspapers of general information are <i><a href="/wiki/El_Peri%C3%B3dico_de_Catalunya" title="El Periódico de Catalunya">El Periódico de Catalunya</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/La_Vanguardia" title="La Vanguardia">La Vanguardia</a></i>, both with editions in Catalan and Spanish. Catalan only published newspapers include <i><a href="/wiki/Ara_(newspaper)" title="Ara (newspaper)">Ara</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Punt_Avui" class="mw-redirect" title="El Punt Avui">El Punt Avui</a></i> (from the fusion of <i><a href="/wiki/El_Punt" title="El Punt">El Punt</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Avui" title="Avui">Avui</a></i> in 2011), as well as most part of the local press. The Spanish newspapers, such as <i><a href="/wiki/El_Pa%C3%ADs" title="El País">El País</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">El Mundo</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/La_Raz%C3%B3n_(Madrid)" title="La Razón (Madrid)">La Razón</a></i>, can be also acquired.
</p><p>Catalonia has a long tradition of use of radio, the first regular regular radio broadcast in the country was from Ràdio Barcelona in 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Today, the public <a href="/wiki/Catalunya_R%C3%A0dio" title="Catalunya Ràdio">Catalunya Ràdio</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Corporaci%C3%B3_Catalana_de_Mitjans_Audiovisuals" title="Corporació Catalana de Mitjans Audiovisuals">Catalan Media Corporation</a>) and the private <a href="/wiki/RAC_1" title="RAC 1">RAC 1</a> (belonging to Grup Godó) are the two main radios of Catalonia, both in Catalan.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG/220px-Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG/330px-Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG/440px-Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Festival_Internacional_de_Cinema_de_Catalunya_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sitges_Film_Festival" title="Sitges Film Festival">Sitges Film Festival</a> of 2009</div></div></div>
<p>Regarding the cinema, after the democratic transition, three styles have dominated since then. First, auteur cinema, in the continuity of the <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_School_of_Film" title="Barcelona School of Film">Barcelona School</a>, emphasizes experimentation and form, while focusing on developing social and political themes. Worn first by <a href="/wiki/Josep_Maria_Forn" title="Josep Maria Forn">Josep Maria Forn</a> or <a href="/wiki/Bigas_Luna" title="Bigas Luna">Bigas Luna</a>, then by <a href="/wiki/Marc_Recha" title="Marc Recha">Marc Recha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Rosales" title="Jaime Rosales">Jaime Rosales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Serra" title="Albert Serra">Albert Serra</a>, this genre has achieved some international recognition. Then, the <a href="/wiki/Documentary" class="mw-redirect" title="Documentary">documentary</a> became another genre particularly representative of contemporary Catalan cinema, boosted by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Joaquim_Jord%C3%A0_i_Catal%C3%A0&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Joaquim Jordà i Català (page does not exist)">Joaquim Jordà i Català</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Guer%C3%ADn" title="José Luis Guerín">José Luis Guerín</a>. Later, horror films and thrillers have also emerged as a specialty of the Catalan film industry, thanks in particular to the vitality of the <a href="/wiki/Sitges_Film_Festival" title="Sitges Film Festival">Sitges Film Festival</a>, created in 1968. Several directors have gained worldwide renown thanks to this genre, starting with Jaume Balagueró and his series <i><a href="/wiki/REC_(film)" title="REC (film)">REC</a></i> (co-directed with Valencian Paco Plaza), <a href="/wiki/Juan_Antonio_Bayona" class="mw-redirect" title="Juan Antonio Bayona">Juan Antonio Bayona</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_orfanato" class="mw-redirect" title="El orfanato">El Orfanato</a></i> or <a href="/wiki/Jaume_Collet-Serra" title="Jaume Collet-Serra">Jaume Collet-Serra</a> with <i><a href="/wiki/Orphan_(2009_film)" title="Orphan (2009 film)">Orphan</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Unknown_(2011_film)" title="Unknown (2011 film)">Unknown</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Non-Stop_(film)" title="Non-Stop (film)">Non-Stop</a></i>.
</p><p>Catalan actors have shot for Spanish and international productions, such as <a href="/wiki/Sergi_L%C3%B3pez_(actor)" title="Sergi López (actor)">Sergi López</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Museum_of_Cinema_-_Tom%C3%A0s_Mallol_Collection&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Museum of Cinema - Tomàs Mallol Collection (page does not exist)">Museum of Cinema - Tomàs Mallol Collection</a> (Museu del Cinema - Col.lecció Tomàs Mallol in Catalan) of Girona is home of important permanent exhibitions of cinema and pre-cinema objects. Other important institutions for the promotion of cinema are the <a href="/wiki/Gaud%C3%AD_Awards" title="Gaudí Awards">Gaudí Awards</a> (Premis Gaudí in Catalan, which replaced from 2009 Barcelona Film Awards themselves created in 2002), serving as equivalent for Catalonia to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Goya_Awards" title="Goya Awards">Goya</a> or French <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Award" title="César Award">César</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philosophy">Philosophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Philosophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Seny" title="Seny">Seny</a></div>
<p><i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">Seny</i> is a form of ancestral Catalan wisdom or sensibleness. It involves well-pondered perception of situations, level-headedness, awareness, integrity, and right action. Many Catalans consider seny something unique to their culture, is based on a set of ancestral local customs stemming from the scale of values and social norms of their society.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Catalonia" title="Sport in Catalonia">Sport in Catalonia</a></div>
<p>Sport has an important incidence in Catalan life and culture since the beginning of the 20th century and, as a result, it has a well developed sport infraestructure. The main sports are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handball" title="Handball">handball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rink_hockey" class="mw-redirect" title="Rink hockey">rink hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Motorsport" title="Motorsport">motorsport</a>.
</p><p>Despite the fact that the most popular sports are represented outside by the Spanish national teams, Catalonia can officially play as itself in some others, like <a href="/wiki/Korfball" title="Korfball">korfball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Most of Catalan Sports Federations have a long tradition and some of them participated in the foundation of international sports federations, as the Catalan Federation of Rugby, that was one of the founder members of the <a href="/wiki/FIRA_%E2%80%93_Association_of_European_Rugby" class="mw-redirect" title="FIRA – Association of European Rugby">Fédération Internationale de Rugby Amateur</a> (FIRA) in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-fira-aer-rugby.com_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fira-aer-rugby.com-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The majority of Catalan sport federations are part of the <a href="/wiki/Sports_Federation_Union_of_Catalonia" title="Sports Federation Union of Catalonia">Sports Federation Union of Catalonia</a> (Catalan: <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">Unió de Federacions Esportives de Catalunya</i>), founded in 1933.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Football_Federation" title="Catalan Football Federation">Catalan Football Federation</a> also periodically fields a <a href="/wiki/Catalonia_national_football_team" title="Catalonia national football team">national team</a> against international opposition, organizing friendly matches. In the recent years they have played with Bulgaria, Argentina, Brazil, Basque Country, Colombia, Nigeria, Cape Verde and Tunisia. The biggest football clubs are <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> (also known as Barça), who have won five European Cups (<a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>), and <a href="/wiki/RCD_Espanyol" title="RCD Espanyol">RCD Espanyol</a>, who have twice been runner-up of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a>. Both play in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>.
</p><p>The Catalan <a href="/wiki/Waterpolo" class="mw-redirect" title="Waterpolo">waterpolo</a> is one of the main powers of the Iberian Peninsula. The Catalans won triumphs in waterpolo competitions at European and world level by club (the Barcelona was champion of Europe in 1981/82 and the Catalonia in 1994/95) and national team (one gold and one silver in Olympic Games and World Championships). It also has many international <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" class="mw-redirect" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> champions.
</p><p>Motorsport has a long tradition in Catalonia, which involving many people, with some world champions and several competitions organized since the beginning of the 20th century. The <a href="/wiki/Circuit_de_Catalunya" class="mw-redirect" title="Circuit de Catalunya">Circuit de Catalunya</a>, built in 1991, is one of the main motorsport venues, holding the Catalan motorcycle Grand Prix, the Spanish F1 Grand Prix, a DTM race, and several other races.
</p><p>Catalonia hosted many relevant international sport events, such as the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> in Barcelona, and also the <a href="/wiki/1955_Mediterranean_Games" title="1955 Mediterranean Games">1955 Mediterranean Games</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2013_World_Aquatics_Championships" title="2013 World Aquatics Championships">2013 World Aquatics Championships</a> or the <a href="/wiki/2018_Mediterranean_Games" title="2018 Mediterranean Games">2018 Mediterranean Games</a>. It held annually the fourth-oldest still-existing <a href="/wiki/Cycling_stage_race" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycling stage race">cycling stage race</a> in the world, the <a href="/wiki/Volta_a_Catalunya" title="Volta a Catalunya">Volta a Catalunya</a> (Tour of Catalonia).<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 235px"><div style="width: 235px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbols">Symbols</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Symbols">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/National_symbols_of_Catalonia" title="National symbols of Catalonia">National symbols of Catalonia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Senyera_(Pl._Octavi%C3%A0,_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg/220px-Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg/330px-Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg/440px-Senyera_%28Pl._Octavi%C3%A0%2C_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Senyera_(Pl._Octavi%C3%A0,_S._Cugat_del_Vall%C3%A8s)_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Senyera" title="Senyera">Flag of Catalonia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Catalonia has its own representative and distinctive national symbols such as:<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>The flag of Catalonia, called the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Senyera" title="Senyera">Senyera</a></i>, is a <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_vexillology#Flag_identification_symbols" title="Glossary of vexillology">vexillological symbol</a> based on the heraldic emblem of <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Barcelona" class="mw-redirect" title="Counts of Barcelona">Counts of Barcelona</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> of the Crown of Aragon, which consists of four red stripes on a golden background. It has been an official symbol since the Statute of Catalonia of 1932.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/National_Day_of_Catalonia" title="National Day of Catalonia">National Day of Catalonia</a><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> is on 11 September, and it is commonly called <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">la Diada</i>. It commemorates the 1714 <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Barcelona_(1713%E2%80%931714)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Barcelona (1713–1714)">Siege of Barcelona</a> defeat during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>.</li>
<li>The national anthem of Catalonia is <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Els_Segadors" title="Els Segadors">Els Segadors</a></i> and was written in its present form by Emili Guanyavents in 1899. The song is official by law from 25 February 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> It is based on the events of 1639 and 1640 during the <a href="/wiki/Reapers%27_War" title="Reapers&#39; War">Catalan Revolt</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Day#St._George&#39;s_Day_in_Catalonia" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Day">St George's Day</a> (<i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">Diada de Sant Jordi</i>) is widely celebrated in all the towns of Catalonia on 23 April, and includes an exchange of books and roses between couples or family members.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Catalan_cuisine" title="Catalan cuisine">Catalan cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg/220px-Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg/330px-Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg/440px-Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="732" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet_-_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet" title="Pa amb tomàquet">Pa amb tomàquet</a></i> (bread with tomato)</div></div></div>
<p>Catalan gastronomy has a long culinary tradition. Various local food recipes have been described in documents dating from the fifteenth century. As with all the cuisines of the Mediterranean, Catatonian dishes make abundant use of <a href="/wiki/Fish_as_food" title="Fish as food">fish</a>, seafood, <a href="/wiki/Olive_oil" title="Olive oil">olive oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bread" title="Bread">bread</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vegetables" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetables">vegetables</a>. Regional specialties include the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Pa_amb_tom%C3%A0quet" title="Pa amb tomàquet">pa amb tomàquet</a></i> (bread with tomato), which consists of bread (sometimes toasted), and <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomato</a> seasoned with olive oil and salt. Often the dish is accompanied with any number of sausages (cured <a href="/wiki/Botifarra" title="Botifarra">botifarres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuet" title="Fuet">fuet</a>, iberic ham, etc.), ham or cheeses. Others dishes include the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Cal%C3%A7otada" class="mw-redirect" title="Calçotada">calçotada</a></i>, <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Escudella_i_carn_d%27olla" title="Escudella i carn d&#39;olla">escudella i carn d'olla</a></i>, <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text">suquet de peix</i> (fish stew), and a <a href="/wiki/Dessert" title="Dessert">dessert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_cream" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan cream">Catalan cream</a>.
</p><p>Catalan vineyards also have several <i lang="ca" title="Catalan language text"><a href="/wiki/Denominaci%C3%B3n_de_origen" title="Denominación de origen">Denominacions d'Origen</a></i> wines, such as: <a href="/wiki/Priorat_(DOQ)" title="Priorat (DOQ)">Priorat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montsant_DO" title="Montsant DO">Montsant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pened%C3%A8s_(DO)" title="Penedès (DO)">Penedès</a> and <a href="/wiki/Empord%C3%A0_(DO)" title="Empordà (DO)">Empordà</a>. There is also a sparkling wine, the <a href="/wiki/Cava_(Spanish_wine)" title="Cava (Spanish wine)">cava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Catalonia is internationally recognized for its fine dining. Three of <a href="/wiki/The_World%27s_50_Best_Restaurants" title="The World&#39;s 50 Best Restaurants">The World's 50 Best Restaurants</a> are in Catalonia,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> and four restaurants have three <a href="/wiki/Michelin_Guide" title="Michelin Guide">Michelin</a> stars, including restaurants like <a href="/wiki/El_Bulli" title="El Bulli">El Bulli</a> or <a href="/wiki/El_Celler_de_Can_Roca" title="El Celler de Can Roca">El Celler de Can Roca</a>, both of which regularly dominate international rankings of restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twinning_and_covenants">Twinning and covenants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalonia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Twinning and covenants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
